When the eyes are open everywhere, and there is no disturbance in the nose, nor diminishment, it means that you should bind the patient; then put a poultice, then apply cupping glasses or heated irons to suck out, then place on the eye .i. make a paste of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolle, and then hold the eye steady, and wrap with bandages and drapery; and the way of draping is that you take drapes quite soft, and double each one in .iiij., and then place one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eyes need most; then hold it steady with a firm bandage above, and reapply the cupping glasses to suck out without piercing; then remove the cupping glasses and let the eye stay steady day and night, and if they become weak, it means you should strain them more; then remove the binding after day and night, and if you see the eye recovering, that is good; if not, then reapply the poultice and drapery and the binding and cupping glasses until it is healthy.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	because of the tearing of the veiled membrane
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come to the veiled membrane, then open, and come forth with papers as if .i. grains of resin, and it is astonishing to see; then if you have seen the veil covered, the operations are such that you put a needle in the root of the part beneath, just below the pupil; then put another needle where there is .i. double thread of the part of the eyelid; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the disposition; then cover the eye with double thread and tie one part of the veil around, and hold it well, then remove the needle and place on the eye a clean moist cloth in abundance of egg whites; and let it be until the threads stick with the veil, then cure the eye with comforting things as long as the wound is healthy; and never restrain the wound by the veil any part of a circle of drapery, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes take on a great appearance, if they pierce through the subtle spatula which comes from the front of the eye, and corrects the moist albumentous and descends to the eyes, and goes in between at once; then it is extracted until it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the cavity of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is not but a bubble that forms in the eye, appearing as a water descending, and it's not really a water; and the manner of appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on a prepared seat and straight, then take the head between your hands from both parts, and move it until you see the bubble coming up to your eyes; then be fixed, and do not descend or disassemble the light, and see the patient's things as they alone can; and if it does not descend below, know that it's a water, and if the descents of the bubble are not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Here is the translation:
des aigues de l’oil	of the humors of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the similarities of the wounds in the division, and that which is necessary to perceive; if one operates according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you place the patient between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and hold the healthy eye firmly and strongly; then put the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are left-handed, or in your right hand if the eyes are right-handed; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left-handed, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eyes are right-handed; then put the point of the instrument on the crown by the thickness of a hair in that white part of the eye at the minor corner, then apply the instrument called "almagda" skillfully, and turn your hand until it penetrates into the white part of the eye, and feel that almagda reaches the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way of almagda be at the depth of the measure of the spaces which are from the prunele to the end of the blackness; and this is the crown of the eye; if you will see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the curved fabric, and then put the instrument next to where the wound is, then press down one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	Here is the translation:
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest, the patient rises by the second route, puts fire with the instrument, and when it is thus fixed and does not ascend, then extracts the almond-shaped tumor lightly in turning the hand little by little; and then puts back into the aigue a little of the gemstone, and leaves from that the eye within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then puts by default the eyes besmeared or anointed with rose oil and in abundance of egg white, and binds with the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our kind, put on a common poultice with an abundance of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond oil cannot enter the eye because of its thickness, for there are some men who have very hard eyelashes, so it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", whose form is this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce then the conjunctive sorely, and do not move too much in the background, but make the subtle eye, then extract the almond-shaped tumor, as we have said; and at the completion of the work appearing to the patient who is asleep, in which he sleeps on his back in the darkened room; and be deprived of all movements, and take light food, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and be tied according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in that same darkened house, and test his sight, and make him see certain things, and then put back the bandage until the seventh day; and it is not suitable that you do this at the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is suitable that you delay this, because the aigue ascends hastily.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	Here is the translation:
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then it happens little by little in his case; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	Here is the translation:
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the forms of algmada, because those who do not know them go astray; and thus they are properly aligned:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And thus the head of the bone is in this subtle complexity, and the last one at four angles aqueous.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh over the nails
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No times do birthmarks or moles appear in various ways, because there are some that resemble scorptions with many feet; and if there is such a one where the flesh has changed to a flux color, and if it has soft flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of these moles which are soft and not changed, you must make the patient sit between your hands against the sun; and open their nostrils, and cast the onion at those moles, and remove their roots; for you can then sustain with a subtle spatula on one side, until you know that the mole is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be coped with, if you open everything .i. of the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if without surgical intervention, or an abscess bursts, if you sew it up as it should be; and if they are malignant abscesses, if you hurry and cauterize until the blood is stanched and all the wounds are closed, then pour in water or vinegar and sharp wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the mole does not open and moisture comes up to the palace, know that it is healthy; and if moisture does not pass as it should, know that there is a new mole above, which does not come from cutting: then you must thread the linen on a small needle, and be careful with our hands, and have at least an inch of space between each hand; and place the patient's head in the filth of their nose, and draw out the odor as it comes through the nose into the mouth; and many times children do this as a game, and it is an easy thing for one who wants to do it; then hold one end that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other while being careful as we are with the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do as much as you know that the ninth has corrupted this flesh, then draw out the thread, suck out the blood, and anoint the thread with Egyptian unguent, and put it back in its place just like before; do this three days or more, until the unguents corrode all that remains of the flesh; and then put on a poultice of plantain for several days until it is healthy, and if there is need of medicines afterwards, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, from which they distill oils and medicines.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or copper, resembling a lamp cover, like a tube, and the conduits are thus; and if you see, make a closed tube, and let the instruments be plain for purging the head; and have .i. a handle on the head to hold it when one heats up the oil or some liquor.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh over the nails
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease occurs on the nails of the hand called "telul", and grows and becomes large, so it is visible to behold; and for this reason you must take care at the beginning, and remove all further, then put on it the cautery or burning medicine; and if you delay taking care until it becomes large, if it is hard, of fixed color, of poor sensation: if you do not touch with iron for it is an encrusted abscess, for when you take care many times, great evil comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of fixed color, and you see that you can remove all, if you cure the patient and take away their fear, and heal the dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nails are cut and burned
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes into one of these cartilaginous joints, it profits little, because in some homes.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary then to cancel what has happened to none, if you see that the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then adjust the two lips of a gash, and treat until it is healthy; and if the lips are already separated from one part and another, it is necessary that you scrape all parts of their skin until they heal, then assemble the two lips together, and hold them in place, and sprinkle with powder of dragon's blood, and incense bruised; and put on the powders a piece of strong or other suitable plaster, and let it stick by itself, then treat with ointment until it is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of the suturing is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or by thread, as I have made you know.
des apostemes des levres	of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At the hands of men who have dens abscesses on their lips, hard, like grains of wheat, and smaller and larger; then it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut into each nut, and take them as pincers, and cover in each part; then apply the lard after the incision of vitriol bruise, so that the blood may be staunched; and then leave it to heal, and cure the lip of dry things until it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times the gums are bruised by a blow, which the old men call "albulus"; if it is necessary that you hold them in place with bandages, and apply a dressing to their root, and let the blood or wound flow; then put on top a vitriol broth or other powders that constrict and dry; and if that wound returns after the incision, and many times happens, if you cover it a second time, and cauterize: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of treatments to heal wounds.
des sordens	of abscesses
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the top of the teeth, deep in the mouth between the gums, scabs which are black and bitter; and sometimes the teeth turn black and yellow and green, until the corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become putrid; if it is necessary that you examine the patient between your hands, and their jaws are in your saint, and take out the teeth or scabs appearing, until nothing remains; and thus make an end to the blackness and the verdor, and the jaundice and other taints, until they are cleared; and if one removes what is at the first root, it is good; if not, then recommence to re-treat on the second day and the third, until you have removed everything; and know that teeth have need of various forms of treatments to remove, according to what the work demonstrates, because the roots which are removed from the teeth have other forms than those which are between the teeth; and these forms and others should be well-equipped with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth for its pain that you delay to treat as long as you can, because it should not be done hastily; for it is a very high substance just up to then so one has no excuse to rush.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained by two tractions, it is necessary that you are certain of the teeth of the oil.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the patient feels the pain, and believes it is in the sainted tooth, and makes traction on the good tooth; and however does not depart from the pain for that, as long as the bad one is extracted, for we have already wanted to do it for these healthy ones; and when you are well certain of the teeth of the oil, then it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth with a spatula strongly to ward off the gum on all sides; then move your fingers or subtle tenaculums at first gently and gently, so they are well relaxed, then fix them well; and let the head of the patient be in your sainted position between your knees, and hold it well so it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and insert it gently into each part lightly, and remove it in the same way you did at first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the teeth are perceived and gnashed, it is necessary that you fill them with drapels, where the perforations are; and if you hold subtly as in tongs, so they do not break while holding; and it is necessary to work very carefully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And you do well to be careful not to break it, and leave a part remaining, and return to the patient through the badness of the root, which causes greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And you beware that you do not act thus as the ignorant healers, who through their haste and hardness often break the cartilage, and do not amend what we have recounted; but they come to be afflicted with this great illness due to the roots which remain, or because of the cartilage which they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is decayed, you wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if blood comes out, which often happens, you apply the vitriol ointment; and if that does not work, you cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, which one must adapt to the teeth first, should be long and pointed and have large handles, so they do not slip when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be thick limbs so they do not bend during treatment, and let them be well-made of iron, and let them be held in place by steady muscles.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in the wound, it is necessary that you apply a cotton cloth soaked in warm water on the spot for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the wounds are softened, then apply the tongs called "algefri", which seem to be a beak of a bird; and they should be made thus like a file, and that is their shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to issue into all these tenacillas, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh totally around the root, and you put the instrument called "althali", that is to say scalpel, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and large so that it does not break easily, and if the root jumps through that, it is good; if not, then help with all the instruments, from which the forms come afterwards.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps with this instrument that has twelve rungs, from which it is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments that are in front of the teeth, and of this instrument that resembles large pincers, from which it is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be strong so that they cannot break, and know that many of the teeth's instruments are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise masters subtly find their own instrument, according to what their works and the disease show them, because there are certain diseases where the ancient ones did not teach at all about the instrument for the diversity of wounds; and it does not break in the cartilage or other bones, or it decays, if one searches for the instruments that are needed, which I have told you, and helps with the gestures, from which it is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let it be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, so it does not slip away, but it can hold and remove; and then restore the limb with convenient medicines, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, if you take out all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and its shape is ugly, especially in small women, if it is necessary that you know if the teeth are not after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and one cannot smooth or file: then take the radius; and if it is joined with the tooth, take this instrument which has a similar shape, and is like a small beak, and let it be of iron sharpened to a point.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the small skull and small hands hold it firmly for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then file it with a part of the file as it is in shape.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file of which one makes the needles; and file the small tooth firmly but gently with small hands, so that it does not move until it is steady; then smooth it out at the end without any roughness, and if the teeth are too sharp and they bite the tongue, then file the asperity until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when they prick
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth is dislodged, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it so that they do not bite, and you have treated them with constricting medicines, but it does not work; if you need to restrain it with a golden thread, because the silver thread turns green and rotten, but gold does not move at all; and let the medium-sized thread be neither too large nor too small, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you want to adjust the teeth, take the thread and pass it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the teeth among the bad ones, if there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then recommence the covering up to the part where you began, and hold your hand subtly and steadily, so that it does not move at all; and let your treatment be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the heads of the thread to a tourniquet, and assemble them, and place them between the healthy tooth, and adjust it so it does not hurt the tongue; and then leave it thus tightened as much as it can stay, and if it dislocates, or the threads break, hold with another thread; if it stays and serves thus all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the adjustment of the two healthy teeth, and of the two muscles, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, put it back in its place, little by little, as we have said; and do not meddle with it who is not skilled and suffers, and never make the shape of a tooth of ivory from a cow, and put it in the place where the defect is, and hold it thus as we have said, and it will stay and serve thus long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	from the copper of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	It never happens that these threads come from under the tongue or nature, which you do not know thus; or by accident of a wounded abscess; and the operations are such that you open the mouth of the patient, and hold their head in your healthy one, and lift the tongue; then take the nervous thread of the large size, so that the tongue is dislocated from its holding, and if it has hardness or numbness, and it is suddenly wounded, if you find the uncinate and take the large ligament; and beware that the fissure is not too deep, for the artery which is underneath; and when you have done, lift the lever of warm rose water and of cold, then put under the tongue a linen compress; and anoint the patient every night, so that their jaws cannot close.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the flow of blood comes, then apply the glass vessel bruised; and if it does not stop, then cauterize with a slow fire, which is good for this; then treat with another treatment until it is healthy.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see the color of the fuse is black or dark, if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it declines to a blister, and there is moisture, if you pour in an ointment, and you make a subtle spatula, and you deliver from one part and another; and if the blood does not come to your work, if you put on a vitriol broiet as long as it is stained, then return to your work as much as you treat everything fully; then lift up the limb of the axis and of the seat, and cure other cures until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there come abscesses in the throat called "godath", and they are properly called II amandres; when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healthy, beware: if it is a hard aposteme with little sense and a dark color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also because of the flow of blood; but let it be until it becomes ripe, and then you will cut it, or it would break by itself; and if it is of white color and the root is subtle, prepare the instrument to cover, but first make sure the aposteme has cooled down and is quiet.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his head should be in good health, and he should open his mouth and hold the sergeants between his hands, and press the tongue underneath to all the instruments, because this is the method; and it should be of silver or subtle iron, as if a small knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Here is the translation:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then take a candle, because it is its form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be cutting from one part, and naming from the other part; and when you have cut into one of the veins, then cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot and cold water, and if there is a flow of blood, then gargle the patient with hot water, or scorching pommes grenades that are cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the wound is stained; then cure it until it is healthy; and no other time do abscesses grow in the throat besides these two veins, if you cut them thus as the two veins agree.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was growing inside her throat, it's known as a small abscess; and it had almost closed off the entire throat, so the woman could not breathe through the passage that was obstructed, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained like that for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had nearly put out two veins through the two nostrils of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then, and inserted a lancet in one nostril, then the flow of blood was abundant; then I made another incision in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards I inserted the lancet into the abscess, and removed a part of it, and only a little blood came out; and thus the passage of the throat was cleared for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease from cutting away at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess recurred again, and refilled the void I had made, so much that it became very large; then I ignited it and cauterized it deep in the throat: thus it did not grow again; and I parted from those regions, and knew only God could do something about it after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the vein descends to the skin, and it is swollen and long, then it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is rather thick and round, then it is called an "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the inflamed abscess is appeased, and it is subtle, then it must be coped; and the one that is round and assembled and not long; and it is sanguine or of dark color or black, then it must be eschewed from incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary, therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument which we have mentioned before; then prick the vein with a needle, and draw from below, and cope with one of the two instruments that I have said for incising the two veins.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the surplus which is beyond the natural terminus; for if you cut further, it grieves the voice and the speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two manders, and cure until it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear about cutting, then it is necessary that you use gentleness in the cauterization of the sensitive areas with fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cautery is to be sharply pointed.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head in your healthy hand, and then presses the tongue to the instrument which we have said or chapter of cautery, and confirms with a sharp living flame, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in employing the management of this instrument, from which it is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, not like cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calament and ysope and origanum and rue and camomille and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in a pot, and put them to boil, and make the pot well glued with strong earth, and let it have an instrument that cuts according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether of silver or of iron, and whether one of the heads is thrust into the patient's mouth as far as the vapor rises to the eye through the vein, so that the eye is mortified; after often recommencing, so that the eye becomes dry, and beware that you do not do this at the beginning of the onset of the hot abscess, because many things happen; and do not do it unless at the decline of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put a small hook of egg whites in the chief, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot; for the hook of egg whites does not let the vapor grievously harm the mouth, and it is a good cure altogether healthy.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it happens at the throat or spine of a fish, or some other thing; so therefore you should try what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing; and what does not appear and is rejected in the throat, therefore you should make the patient vomit thus that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps by chance the thing will be cleared by vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of turnip, or a root of lettuce, or a crumb of dry bread; and tie it to the sponge thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will be rejected, and then you will extract it again; and if it does not come out from what we have said, take this instrument of a plectron in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so they can enter more lightly into the throat, and hold the head high elevated; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all does not go well, nor does it bulge inward; and it is of great value that the patient holds the instrument, because it is held or the thing is at ease; if it holds below, where it draws everything equally throughout the entire instrument, so it is drawn.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the sensibility of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	No medicine is suitable for the blood, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not benefit at all, then look into the patient's throat in the sun, then press the tongue to the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound, so treat it thoroughly with small incisions, or subtle tenure that are worth it.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a heated iron, and insert it into the patient's throat, then apply the heating of the iron to the spot, and make it sweat.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And tease the patient with water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full view of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in so that it swallows, and move it with its own hand often; and if soon as the wound feels the water, it scabs.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not scab as we have said, then suffumigate the patient with assaftide, with the instrument that I said in the fumigation of the urine; do this many times, for it will heal without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot where there are visible coals, and let it be covered with a perforated lid in the middle, and in this pierced lid is the head of the instrument; then you throw in the fumigation, and the patient puts the end of the cane into his mouth, and closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but reaches just to the sanies; and the sanies will now descend, and if they do not fall, then recommence the fumigation many times; and the patient suffers thirst, and eats salty and bitter things, and drinks no water; and then it is necessary that it be driven out by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the wound is such that when one can see it, it resembles curved tongs entering into the throat; and it has a resemblance to a beak of a sign, and it has roughness of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and see here the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the cauterizing irons for abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many abscesses are similar, according to what the remembrance brings hereafter in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and it is in two manners, one of which is in its own resemblance, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the joints where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the flesh are different from those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that one should not pierce, as long as the bowels are ripe according to their accomplishment; and if there are those that require piercing when they are ripe, and do not die according to their accomplishment, like abscesses that are near the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near the joints, and one leaves them until they are ripe inside, perhaps if the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is near the principal member, and you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal member; or if it is near the foundation, one should pierce it in such a way that it is ripe; and it is not suitable to pierce a ripe abscess without complete digestion, except for the one that is near the foundation, so that it does not putrefy inside, and becomes fistulous, and cannot be healed within a long period.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the signs of the perforation of the abscess which is ripe according to completion, and it's when the pain is alleviated, and the departure from fever, and the lessening of the pain and of the redness, and the debating and settling of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation sit or more depending on the abscess, and where it appears most; and let the perforation be from the length of the body, and if the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all their equalities where there is no polypus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases where they swell, by stretching according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the flesh, it is better that you let the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce before that, the body would be filled with much filth from him, and it is full of much foulness; and by chance they harden the lips and the depths of him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there are any abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limbs have need of.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you make small incisions for small abscesses, small perforations; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many fissures according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to shave the skin, and cover; when it has become thus as I dress, and is amortized, it is necessary to do thus as one does for blisters: and if there are those that are cut into three angles, and if there are those that one covers like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the loins; and if there are those where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head of a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it plainly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has collected great matter, and you pierce it, so do not remove all the matter at once, but take part of it; then stop the abscess until another day, then take out nothing more; do this many times, a little at a time, until the matter is all gone; similarly if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the surgeon often kills the patient with the issue of the matter, which happens by misadventure, and you do not perceive it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Abandon then this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, heal the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain cut, apply a tent of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, it is necessary that you put a tent in each one so they do not touch each other; and if you have caught in the abscess a piece of skin, and you have sewn it around, it is necessary that you fill it with much cotton or dressing of flax thread without moisture, and leave it until the third day; then remove it, and cure with ointment as long as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if you remove blood that comes from your work, if you handle it with cold and ease, and soften the dressing, and put it on the limb that is being treated many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you remove blood that persists, you handle it with governance and care, and the powders that I have mentioned in my book, and if it's during winter, and the limbs or abscesses are very nervous, then you must put on warm and moist dressings with wine and hot oil; and if it's in summer, and the limbs are cold, then you must put on warm and moist dressings with water and hot oil, or with cold wine and oil, just until the third day, as we have said; and then separate the abscess and the fluid and the cure, as it is necessary, until they are healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to understand universally in the treatment of abscesses: for you have said how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and see this chapter.
des soros	of ulcers
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the crust of a new abscess forms, and there are mannerisms that are in tiles, just as the joiner of a vein, and much is similar.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There is fat and such things where there is moisture, just as in pores; and if there are such things that are hard and rocky to the cutter, and there is no doubt if the artery does not act contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of the cut are so that you experience all the instrument called "entromissoire", from which the form comes hereafter, whatever thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then they make it by drying above a length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, then they scrape without leaving anything behind the skin that contains that moisture, for it returns immediately when one leaves nothing; then inserts cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and in vinegar, and applies to the wound, and leaves it until the next day; and this corrects what has been delayed from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then recauterize the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain at all in pain; then heal the wound of pricking with a suitable remedy, so that it becomes healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscesses hold in a fat nut, so cut according to this form, from afar; and you remove the skin, and scrape off all around, and put all your treatment to draw forth the pus that is there; and if the artery makes you do the opposite, so do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And thus do with the abscess if it is piercing, and how to cut and how to cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut into the piercing abscess and the moist one, it is lighter, for they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or heads where there is no moisture, and among these I treated an old woman's head; and found the abscess just like a dry, rough, and bluish stone, which could not be broken; and even if one had made any effort, it would have been just as well to make a wound like a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming onto the head, just like those that come onto the heads of children and the roots of the ears, one should open them up carefully every day, depending on how much they need to be drained; and one should treat them as it is necessary.
des scrophules	of the scalp ulcers
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and beneath the shoulders, and in the groin area, and sometimes they come from another part or limb, and are numerous, and are intertwined with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each abscess is properly located within its side, just like the tumor and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the similarities of these abscesses are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that case where you see a good disposition in the touching, and it is similar to the color of the body, and it moves from each part and is not airy as near the neck or at the artery, and is not very deep; so it is necessary that you cut above, and scrape off each part, and stretch out the two lips of the heart as oncines, if you are a master, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and treat little by little, and be sure that you do not touch the nerve or the vein, and do not let it be too shallow, so you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut into the vein or artery, and this does not allow you to stop, then put vitriol broiet in the wound, or some powders that staunch bleeding, and hold the wound; and let it be until the abscess is softened, and the wound becomes mollified, and begins to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the bleeding is stanched, return to your work, until you complete it; then inquire with your finger whether small scrophulae remain, if you cut and mend them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrophula, it does not seem that you should cut that scrophula at its root, but rather tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall off by itself without harm; then fill the wound with a great deal of cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire tumor, it is necessary that you reassemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, then there will be no excess flesh remaining from the greatness of the tumor.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you understand to cut at the root of it, and to draw out strongly, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those tumors that have excess flesh, pierce where it appears to be dying; and pierce thus as the one mentioned before, depending on it, then amend it with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, then the treatment with ointment will bring forth a scar, until it is healthy.
de squinance	of squinting
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and that is the scripture of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinting, it is necessary that the cutting of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be avoided; and one should not help by that, because all the veins and the pormon of the patient are at risk of having an abscess burst in the mouth, or in the throat or in .ij. mandrels.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the arm, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the loss that comes from strangulation.
