Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary, therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it beneath three circles or four with a small cut across, between the two circles or according to the quantity of the cut across the siphac, not in the cartilage; and if it is convenient at the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long enough to be cleared.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the masters are fearful, then it is necessary that they stretch the skin of the throat to the entire neck, then open the chest as far as it reaches the canal; and clear the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cover the syphac, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the flow of the canal which bursts forth through the broken place, and through the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed during which one doubts the strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound of the heart, and sew entirely without sense of cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, so it may be healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	It is necessary to do this just as much as the throat is entirely stuffed, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and the defect lacks the wing.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cover the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and they inhale through the wound, and thus are saved from death; and for this reason the old man orders to leave the wound open as long as the evil of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four. And then he orders to bind the wound and cure, until it is cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman received the cautery, and it was placed in her throat, and part of the sinew from the arm; and I was called upon to cure her, and I found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and knew well that she had not been treated properly, nor had a vein been conducted further than the throat, and the veins were issuing forth through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened to her, and kissed the wound, and cured her until she was healthy; and the young woman did not have further trouble, for her voice returned, and she recovered her disposition; because I saw that in the tailoring of the epiglottis there was no more fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "throat hernia", and it is a large abscess in the color of a jaundice, and it is very common in women; and it is classified into two manners: natural, and accidental; or natural has no point of injury.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental is classified into two manners, one of which resembles a fatty tumor, and the other manner resembles an abscess that comes from our artery; and there is fear, and it does not require making false fires except in those who are small, and it proves and searches for all the internal passages: if you find it thus as I do not have a fat tumor, and it does not penetrate into any vein, then you cover it, just like one covers the tumors, and you extract it from its entire cofin, if there is no point; and search thoroughly, and cure it as it requires, until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue. dou chancre	Do you mean "Where cautery"?

And the operations, when it is on the skin or where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile several times; then make him healthier if he has shown signs of repletion, then perform the operation .i. cut into the limb to do the operation; then pour out all your incisions or ulcers, and shave all parts, and scrape all parts without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow freely, and hold the skin well with your hand or with something, and if the remnants of blood make you hesitate about the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize so that the blood is stanched; then treat with another treatment until he is healthy.
de ydropisie	of hydropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division the similarities of hydropsy, and how the assembly of the water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done with medicines, and that which is cured by iron: it is clarified only; and one should not touch iron for these two similarities: that is to know, tympanites and yposarche, because it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this similarity of hydropsy called "clarified" with medicines, and the cure does not benefit, if you see the patient is weak, or if they have another illness besides hydropsy, such as thirst and solution of stomach and similar things; if you do not touch iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient has strong virtue, and they have no other illness except hydropsy only, and it is not too young nor too old, then you must operate: lift the patient straight up with your hands, and the ministers press the stomach at the lowest part of the pis, then take the spinal instrument in this form.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let there be cutting of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And a point, and let it not be so internal that it cannot reach the intestine when one pushes it in, and it cannot become blocked; then see if the dropsy is turning towards the intestines: if it needs to be opened from the belly on the right side of the third rib; and if it is for liver disease, let the opening be on the left side of the third rib; and if it is for the spleen, let it be on the right, and it does not need that the patient's gaze falls on the opening so the superfluous fluids do not run to the weak spot; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and the belly, and lift your hand to the entire space between the skin and the membrane as in scraping a quantity of an ounce or finger; then pierce the membrane until the space comes into view, and it is the place of the water, then draw it forth, and I put away this instrument from what form it is.

de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Here is the translation:
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not mention the circumcision of their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greater part of my masters and wise men who performed circumcision in this way, and with great force, and all in a new manner; if the courses were changed because there are two modes, and by chance one copes on that which is above and delays that which is below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut. De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the mending which is done with great force, I have found the benefit of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well above as below.

dou retenement de l’urine	because of the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief. des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder

de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the ways of stone, and the extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone in the kidney as it rains, and all the signs, and in which stone one must operate by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is in the bladder often affects children, and it's a sign that the water jumps from the bladder with subtle clarity; and it openly hurts, and greatly troubles the penis, and they often fall ill, and then become swollen; and many of these symptoms are foundational; and it's easy to cure children until they are three years old, and it's very grievous in old people, and it's as if midway, for those who are between youth and old age; and it's easier to cure those who have large stones than those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient by cleansing, in order to expel all the bad humors that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders the healing of the wound.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and make them bend and move to the bottom, so that the wound descends to the front of the bladder, and often falls from the high place; then have them sit between your hands prepared, and their hands are below their thighs, so that the bladder is entirely declined downwards; then examine and touch inside; if you feel the wound in the space, hasten now to cut into the wound.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not reach the touching of everything, if you anoint your right index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is old, or your middle finger, if the patient is young and accomplished; and apply it to its foundation, and examine the wound, and when you feel it with your finger, if you massage at the neck of the bladder; then press on your finger, and apply it to the depth where you see fit to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to stretch out his right hand above the loins, and with his left hand touch the skin that is beneath the loins in the area where one makes the incision; then he should apply the spatula-like instrument, because this is its form.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make between what is between the hip and the fundament, not in the middle but at the side of the left thigh; and let it be straight on the stone, and the two should be together or fundament, and let the waist be so traversed that it is wide by default, and inside narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; perhaps the press if the two which are in the fundament, that it feels no painful labor; and know that there is a part of the stone where it has angles, and margins: if it is difficult to extract; and if a part which is underneath, similar to a pebble, and round, whose issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	If there is a part where it has angles and margins, make the waist larger; and if it does not feel, it is necessary that you extract at the handles which are like a lime at the head, to extract the stone so it does not break; or you put beneath the subtle curved instrument at the head; and if you cannot engineer thus, if you enlarge the little hole, and if the blood does not flow, if you extract with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, if you first remove the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then pull strongly, and the small ones afterwards if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, you must cauterize it, and make a bigger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Because these things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes out through his bed because the wounds cannot heal; but you must exert yourself to treat it, or to dissect the tendons, as much as you can treat it by pieces; and when you have completed your work, if you fill the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it steady, and put on a dressing of soft cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then resolve the patient back onto his bed, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you remove it, rub in very well the oil and water, then apply the ointment of Dyafinicon and Basilicon ointment, until he is healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses come into the wound and ulcers, and congealments of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by this means that without a flow with the urine: then put your finger in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrode the bladder, and putrefy; then lift the wound with water and salt and silk, and aid him in all ways that you can, as long as he is healthy; and it is necessary that all the wounds that you cure, that you bind the two thighs together, and assemble the medicines on the spot.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the kidney is small, and it is conducted by the rod, and fixed in, and the urine cannot flow out; so the treatment of what I say thus, that you should cut frequently, is to excuse the cutting because of this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a forest of iron in this form and let it be at two angled points fixed in the thigh:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	then take the thread and tie it around the rod beneath the kidney, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then insert the rod gently into the rod, until it reaches the kidney; and turn the rod in your hand in the kidney little by little, until you can feel the other side of the kidney; if the urine comes then, press your hand on what remains of the kidney that is inside the rod.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is thus broken, and bursts out with the urine, and cures the patient; and if you cannot do this because of any thing that deflects it, then tie the thread beneath the kidney and another above, then make the rod straight at the spot where the kidney is between the two ligaments, then extract it forcibly, and loosen the ligament, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure until it be sound.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone in women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Sometimes it happens that the stone is in the womb of women, and if it happens often, then the treatment is difficult, and is prevented by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows herself well, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman well skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the stone of the woman is more profound than the stone of the man, because it makes a deeper cut, and great fear there is. And if need be sent to that, then it is necessary that you take a wise woman knowing well, and prick the true vein on, and if you do not find it, then ask I cast subtle gaze; and present a wise woman in the life of women, where a woman who knows part of the art, and commands that she does what you command from the inquiry of the stone; and see very well if the woman is virgin: then it is necessary to bore into her finger or foundation and inquire about the stone; and if she finds it, then constrain beneath her finger, and recommend that she bores into her finger or with the disease, and asks and presses her left hand on the bladder strongly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it is necessary that she moves the skin from the entrance of the bladder up to the root of the thigh, so that it comes to the root of the hip; then feel around the stone in the root of the hip against the middle of the concha, where it appears most apparent, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her finger above the stone or below, and be the first to cut small; then put the razor in the incision, if you feel the stone if it increases the wound so much that the stone may come out, and know that there are many kinds of stones: it is to know, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and which have roots.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the similarities in order to know the exit.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood does not come out, put the vitriol ointment on the place, and hold it for an hour until the blood is stained; then return to your work, so that the stone may be removed, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of the stone as aids to help you in your operation; and if the blood does not come out, and it is from the artery that is cut, put the powder on the place and hold tight with tents and bandages, and do not start again, and leave the stone and do not touch it anymore, lest by chance the patient may die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the flow of blood is calmed, and the veins are purified, then return to your work, so that the stone may be broken.
de hernie carnouse	from a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Here is the translation:
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this arm is from weakness that comes to the joints, and it is spread throughout that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And often if it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: whether it's a declining color to yellow, or without red, or black, or watery pale, and that happens more; and these are the signs of recognizing this assembly, for if it is white or jaundiced as we have said, then the apostemes are ripe, I do not think like the figure of an egg, and does not open the joints, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in its own fabric, then the apostemes are ripe with a part of the egg, and therefore one thinks that it's another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white jaundice, then it feels very well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, then you probe into all the intramuscular quarter, from which the form is thus presented.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the interior quarters, judge of that which is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat with iron, it is necessary that the patient be sound in body and replenished in his flesh; then place him on his back, on something slightly elevated, and put many drapes underneath; then sit on his left side, and instruct the minister to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs of the heart; then take the scalpel, and cut into the skin of the ribs within the length just up to the nail, and make a straight incision in dividing the skin of the ribs up to the white spot, and carefully remove the thin layer according to what you can do; then pierce the white spot with a flow of water at a large opening, and extract all the water, and then put on ointments, and apply the white spot above; and do not touch the heart of the ribs, but let the white spot only be treated; cut everything or in pieces carefully the side of it subtly, so that if you do not treat it wisely, the water will return; and if the vein is full of blood, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the white spot; then assemble the two leaves of the heart of the ribs into a bundle, then treat as for other wounds, until he is sound.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the corrupted vein of another disease, it is necessary that you lift the vessels that are suspended, doubting the flow of blood; then touch the joint to all the suspended, and extract the vein, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the wound is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; if you cut the other part as you did the first equalization, then suck out the blood, and put on the clean wound a soothing ointment of rose oil; and put on another clean wound a soothing ointment of wine and oil, and put on the two bandages, and put double layer drapery, and bind it all together with the string that follows this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two bandages, and apply them with a clean dressing according to this resemblance, and assemble them by sewing on the girdle of the arms, and one of the heads takes hold at the base just up to the back, and another at the part of the handle; and another head takes hold on the two angles, and so is assembled the whole restraint in the loop of the arm; and no medicine is made with this cautery iron in the size of an iron bar, and it is that you take a subtle cautery scalpel, and cut the skin of the bandages, and be careful as we have said, so that the white syfac that contains the wound is discovered; if you take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syfac as oncines, and scrape it with this subtle cautery hot:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And examine in all ways that you can, as long as you stretch everything; and beware that the fires do not touch the skin; and know that this work is more salvaging; and beware of the deterioration of blood, and remember that the operations of cutting are; and if nothing does contrary to you, or an abscess bursts or deteriorates blood or something else, if cure what does contrary to you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful, and does not want to undergo this operation due to its horror, if you make a perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are well certain through the signs that we have said that the watery liquid is there, if you seat the patient on a high chair; then pierce the abscess in the lower part of the entire spatula, and put the perforation from a long cord; and make the opening wide, so that all the water flows out; then put cotton on the wound, and tie it, and let the remaining water flow out, then cure until the wound is healthy; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to issue from the mouth of the wound, it is necessary that you use a pen or instrument with which one extracts the watery liquid of hydropics, whose form is thus before; and enlarge the wound, and know that the watery liquid returns, and is gathered together after six months or within a year, and when it is gathered together as before, and thus the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Be aware that in this chapter there is more fear in many dispositions, because it seems to me that it is of no value unless one lets it be; and I will tell you the work and the appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come to a head, and likewise as wounds; and it is in most cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know by the excessive and bitter humor, which is spread through the veins, or by percussion; and it is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and there is no true pain, and it is a grievous abscess; and sometimes it happens that an abscess is greenish and pungent, and of a dark color, and never comes from a narrowing of the artery, or from inflammation of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is by narrowing of the artery, it is known by the warm disposition of the abscess, when you press it with your fingers; and it is not necessary that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Here is the translation:
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the vein is suddenly swollen with these new flesh, then it is necessary that you treat the vein, and the cup; and if it is attached to the syphac, or in those which are within the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all that tension, and the cup returns.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is where the back skin is, it is necessary that you cut all of it, and withdraw the vein, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the operations are completed, apply the plaster of moist linen oil and rose water, then treat with other treatments until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	These are enclosed abscesses resembling a boil, with the softening of the surrounding tissue, and the patient suffers greatly when it bursts; and the treatment of this disease is very near to being fearful as this one before, and always we will describe the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you seat the patient on a high stool, then bind him with suspensory bands below his thighs, to all the vessels that are near the verge, and tie them firmly, and stretch them out forcibly; then cut away with a spatula trenchant widely to uncover the vessels, until they are discovered, and then strip away from each part, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in temples; then fix a double thread or needle, and bind it at the first joint where the veins come together, and bind it again at the other head; then cut away in a straight line, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupted moistures; then treat the wound as others do, so that no vessel is injured that nourishes one of the surrounding tissue; for by this means there comes no harm, and if all the vessels are visible, it is necessary to treat them at all the vessels; so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment through the incision of the vessels, and dry out and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the treatment of the face
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	Here is the translation:
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the swelling of the section that makes sudden painful beginnings come, and there are diverse abscesses appearing beneath the skin, close by, and it is because of the issue of the intestine and the body's failure due to the swelling.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes it descends with the intestines, and is retained inside, and causes great pain to suffer for the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments with fear, because it is necessary to beware of its effects.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	Here is the translation:
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And at no time is it cauterized, the white thus that we have said, after the incision, due to fear of deterioration of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Here is the translation:
de hernie carnouse	from a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this wound I never saw anyone who dared to make the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done thus, like the scorpion which assembles at the sight, in such a manner that you lift the veins, after adjusting lightly on the joint below; then cut in the middle, and cure the abscess of those who open, until the veins heal; and the cure is as we have said, until it is healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Never at any time does a rupture occur in the entrails, as we have said, and opens the loins; and none of the intestines are cut, and if they are cut, it is little, and repair all hours; and however long it remains in this point, it believes the wound or syphac, until the intestines open; and this happens through the extension of the syphac which is in the entrails, as we have said, because it is extended, then softened and inflamed the loins and opened; and the cure is by cautery, as we have previously said; and never is a cure made with iron in this manner: and it is that the patient places his back between your hands, then cut the loin of the rupture inflated according to the quantity of three fingers; and then extract the syphac which is beneath the skin that has swelled, then take the reasoning and place it on the loin appearing from the syphac; and press at the bottom of the belly, then cut the two loins appearing from the syphac on the head of the reasoning, and cut one and the other; then extract the head of the reasoning, and do not touch any point of the syphac that does not extend to another thing, as I have made you know in the cure of the rupture of the intestines; then the cure through the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the veins, if you make a wound and treat the wound, so that it may be healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The veins are constricted, and have no appearance in the wound, and the cauterers are moved in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the intestines
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the joints is softened in some homes, because the flesh that is within is softened, and it is pleasant to see; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure, to make the patient sit on their back, and cover the softened skin with natural skin; then assemble the .ij. lips to a suture, and if you see, first remove the excess of the softened skin from .iij. sutures or .iiij. firmly; then cover between the sutures, and cure it as with other wounds, until it is healthy, and feels the thread.
dou chastrement	with strengthening
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	I know that cauteries are commended in our law, and for this reason it pleases me not to speak of them in this book; and it is not necessary to make a fuss about it except in two ways: one, where the masters respond when asked about treatment; and the other, because we often have need of chastisement from some beasts to aid us, such as goats and sheep and chatts and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that cauteries are made in two ways: either by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one that we make by attraction, we make the beast sit in hot water, so that its skin becomes softened and pendulous; then take them in your hand, until they are relaxed and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Here is the translation:
des hermofrodites	of the hemorrhoids
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Here is the translation:
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another way is with women, and it is on the little finger as a rod and they grasp it.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment of men and women is that you cut the adjacent flesh all, and treat it as other wounds; in the second way, for men whose urine passes through the skin of the thighs, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of the tenderness
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A pustule is an adjacent flesh on the natural part, as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as big as a hand, and that's the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you remove the superfluous flesh of the pustule with your hand or with onguents, and cut lightly; and do not go too deep in fear that blood vessels may be injured, then the treatment of another wound until it is healthy; and to another sore that grows at the mouth of the thigh, and the graft, and by chance it bursts forth, and resembles a cowe, and for this reason the ancients called it "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you take it, as we have said for the tenderness, and the treatment until it is healthy.
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is when the nature of the woman is not well perceived, or the pertus is small; and it is natural from birth, or accidental due to illness that has come; or it is by chance adjusted, or subtle dou syfac, and it is made deep in the marrows, or in the sides, or below, or whatever; and it affects conception, and childbearing, and by chance the flowers have; and the knowledge of this is through the gaze of the baile.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the stoppings are nearly apparent, then you should apply to your fingers or to the vein.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is subtle dou syfac, and it is nearly at the liver, then hurry, and turn thus: put your two index fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, spreading her legs; then turn the two livers forcefully, so that the subtle dou syfac is round, and is above the stoppings; then take a thread, and roll it in oil, and put it on the place, and guide the woman to hold each joint each day, so that she cannot dislocate.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the skin is hard and thick, it is necessary to apply cups to the affected area resembling a mistletoe leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of a flesh wound, then they suspend the onion and the cup; and if the medicines are staining blood, such as dragon's blood, incense, and assemble abundant dew; then apply a large poultice of plantain, so that the wound cannot suppurate; and thus it will be lengthy, and apply a tent of dry linen; then cure with other cures until it is healthy.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when flesh wounds occur, it is necessary to apply cups according to this method, if there are no abscesses that become inflamed.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that becomes inflamed in the flesh, one should not touch it with iron.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhages are wounds of veins that occur without external injury, and when hemorrhages are old they become habitual; and we have already said in the division the similarities of these, and the signs, and I will say here those that receive cures.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the thigh, when they are deeply rooted in the marrow, and they do not appear to sensation, if it is not a cure by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the marrow, which one can feel, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, then apply the poultice as a bandage, and cover it with its roots, then sprinkle on medicines that restrain blood, such as dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bathe her feet in a cold bath for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if the blood flows out, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and gale, and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he stumbles, it’s good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If this does not work, make him take warm baths on his back and massage the affected limbs gently; then take a cloth, and apply a compress of plantain juice or ague tree juice with old wine, and make him take it lying down.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess breaks, treat the wounded area with ointment until it is healthy; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough, dry scab, so you should cover it as I have said before; and then treat it until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the marrow
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses come to the marrow, such as cancer and piercing abscesses and herpes and estoimenes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other illnesses that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary then that I describe in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the marrow, which is not among the abscesses that burst outward; and if you want to know the work of iron, look to see if the abscesses are agitated at the beginning of their coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce, but make meurer until the pain is appeased; and then make the patient sit on a chair, and have him lean against his back and assemble his feet as parts of the leg; and let his thighs be spread out, and put his arms beneath his knees, and bind them well with a linen bandage; then suck up the fluid from the right side, and I will show you the instrument by which one opens the mouth of the marrow, from which afterwards comes the form; and it is necessary that when you have managed this instrument, that you fix the rule first to know the depth of the marrow, so that what enters from the instrument does not come more deeply than it should, and does not harm the patient; and if the instruments are larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the marrow with drapels, so that the instruments do not grieve; and it is necessary that he puts the cornet of the instrument above, and holds the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when abscesses open, and one feels a soft spot in the hand, then it is necessary to cover the head with a spatula; and when the tumor is empty, then it is necessary to put tent moles on the wound with rose oil or green oil; and put the tent under the marrow and above the marrow and above the clean nettle on the water or bad veins are so cured; then heal afterwards for 2 days of ointment, until they are healthy; and never lift the marrow and wound by clusters of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lilies and long aristology are so cured; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is set in the marrow, then it is necessary that you beware of iron cauterization, but heal it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of the birth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Here is the translation:
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	Here is the translation:

de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the birth of the child upon its feet

de l’enfant mort	of the dead child

And if it is twisted in the belly or in the chest, then you must extract it with the drapery enveloped on the hand; and make the belly or chest, so that the moisture issues forth; and if the other limbs are ossified, and the head remains, then put the balm on your hand deep into the marrow, and treat just to the mouth of the marrow; then you put the ninth or tenth, and treat further; and if the mouth of the marrow is constricted by a hot abscess that has come, then you must not work too hard, but rather administer moist and greasy things; and the administrator places plasters, and so on in a soft mollifying and anointing.

And if the mouth of the marrow is already constricted, we have mentioned the treatment of sternuating, and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not respond to all that we have said, beware that you do not fail in treating; but it must be that which is at the mouth of the marrow, that you apply it to the womb of the woman, then cleanse it with a four-part ointment; if she will conceive and give birth, and will come into fever; but meanwhile, when she conceives thus, a bad odor comes from the stomach and head, and harms the patient.

de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.
