Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is repositioned in its place within the body so that it cannot be seen, if it seeks to extract it entirely; and if you feel it, if you draw it out with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot do so because of the narrowness of the wound, and because of the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or vein, if you make an incision as large as the wound; and extract the arrow if you can, and if it has ears on which it holds, if you cut away the flesh that is attached to the two parts where you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so you can extract it; and carefully ensure that you do not break the arrow, but rather extract it more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, let it remain until the swelling has subsided, then extract it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood counteracts you, if you contradict what we have said about the cure in its chapter; and beware of the incision into the nerve and vein, and engineer it so that you can extract the arrow without danger, whether quickly or slowly, or firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow fell, for it is the greatest aid that it be, and if you cannot, then put him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where it opens into something of it, or the skin is swollen at the spot if one looks or feels around: cut thereupon, so much that the tongs can grasp, and then extract it: if it comes out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand roundly, so that it enters into the bone, and enlarges the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it alone and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if the wood of the arrow is there, cut around the entire wood; and if the wood is cut, and you see to administer cutting, if you administer the instrument that cuts, so that the point of the arrow enters into the notch of the instrument; and then cut out, and if the arrow is notched, cut the instrument to enter the point, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, it is necessary that you cut around the entire flesh where the veins are, so you can, then cure the wound as it is needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrowhead is in the foot or abdomen or bladder or ribcage, and it is close by, and you can operate on it, then operate; and beware of operating on the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound, as that is the task; and treat until it is healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to extract arrows is similar to a bird's beak, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways of them: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the swelling resembles that of a bird's beak, to push at the point of the arrowhead, just as it is its shape.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs for applying heat and for extracting if it is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins from which one bleeds, of which XVI are main ones, that is to say: II veins that are behind the ears, called "herbech"; and II arteries that appear in II temples; and II veins that are in II eyelids of the eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein that is on the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the II gullet veins that are in the neck; and the II veins that are above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich"; and II veins that are beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	Here is the translation:
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the savior is the vein that is between the auricular and anular, and if there are two veins; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is below the curve of the left shin, and the second saphein which is at the ankle of the right shin; and the vein that is called "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The health of the veins that are behind the ears helps against ancient cataracts and migraine; and the quality of the healer, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then hold the patient's neck with one eye, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in their dependent places: take care to give it to your finger, and where you feel the pulse beneath your finger, it is a sign of an inch; then take the lancet, and insert it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand over all the vein above, and cut and the skin and the vein very well, so that the blood flows out as much as you see; then hold and bind, until it is healthy; and I have already said about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Here is the translation:
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The health of the forehead vein is worth as much as the health of the cephalic vein in ancient diseases of the face, and in migraines, and in redness; and the quality is that the patient strains their neck by twisting, so much that the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point on the vein, and hold it with your hand, or another thing, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity that you see; then release the patient's neck, and bind the vein so it is healthy and never bursts from a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Here is the translation:
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The health of the two veins that are in the two arms helps with eyes, and with the tendon, and with redness, and with the orbit in the eye, and with diseases of the face; and the quality of their health is that the patient strains their neck by twisting without any cord, as before; then it heals, and so the health of the traverse, a little above the long flame a little large, for there is no point of burning.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the veins are subtle, perhaps they break; then make correction of the blood, as much as you have mastery over it, and then place it on the cushion, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein, which is not worth an egg, and suffers from being forcibly pulled, and from facial diseases, such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, and especially when it is old; and the quality of the blood is that the patient tightens his neck, then tightens his nose with his left hand, and takes a subtle flame long, and places it in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well enough, and the blood will now begin to flow; and do not go too far forward, and make the blood flow according to need, then leave it for a night, because it is almost completely restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the two veins helps with the narrowing of the artery, and at the beginning of messelerie, and many diseases, and impetigo, and corrosion, and herpes, and similar things; and the quality of the blood is that the patient tightens his neck below one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be above the head of the patient, and the patient sits on a seat, then opens the vein of the arm somewhat widely, then draws out the blood moderately, or as much as necessary; then do another part in the other vein, and releases the ligature, and holds back the veins softly, so the patient does not strangle; and let it be until morning, so the wound may be healthy.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The wisdom of the veins above the lips is recognized by a hole in the mouth, and by decay of the gums, and cracks of the lips, and painful nose and interior.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the health is to make the patient sit in front of you, and hold his neck as I have said; then turn the liver, and look at the two veins, one on the right liver and the other on the left, and they are recognized by being black, and because there are small black veins around them: thus take one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, take the largest of each part, and make the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is a similar manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the health under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The health of the veins that are under the tongue helps after the health of the head, and it is about the constriction of the throat, and the diseases of the eye, and the diseases of the mouth; and the quality of this health is that the patient places himself between your hands before the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks underneath on each side for a black vein: thus take one and the other, and do not insert too far, for underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the cut that one commonly bleeds are healthy in two manners: either by pricking with a flame mirror, or subtly olivary like a cutting trenchant, and is called "anesil"; and they are large and subtle according to the largeness and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the "flaime" widely known, is very renowned, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the obvious veins full of thick blood appearing, and that contain thick blood and turmoil; and this is the form of the flame olivary.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed, and it is for cleansing the subtle veins, where there is subtle citrine blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The bleeding of the basilica, which is one of these veins, aids the illnesses that are beneath the throat, and in the neck, and in the foot, and in the belly; and it is necessary for the bleeder to bleed strongly, and to beware of the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and a lot of blood comes out, it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said; and one should not prick with the flame, but rather cut skillfully like anesil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open clearly, it is necessary that you extract it, and change another; or you want any vein of it, or you bleed in its place in the arm: it opens clearly; and the cope with the flame anesthetized, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the place of the wound, it is necessary also that you extract the arm, so that you touch the place as much as you know the pulse; then feel the place of the skin, and then the arm, and cope with the vein of the flame anesthetized; and beware that you do not strike in the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it spill out high like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is not from an artery: hasten then, and put your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the blood stops; tie up the arm, and leave it so, and do not move the patient; and be without fear, and do not move until they are healthy.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound is not stanched, and it vanishes, and the medicines are not present, then cut the artery so it opens, for the head of the veins; and stanch the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a dressing of fistula, and make it, and take one of the moieties and place it next to the other just so; if the wound is stanched, that's good; if not, apply the treatment, as we have said, with powders that stanch blood; and the stanching is not grievous in many dispositions for the small size of the wound, and the possibility of a lien on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The health of the vein is in the middle if it helps to draw blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of basilica and cephalic, as we have said; and it behooves the healer to be wary of the nerve that is below, and if he presses too hard, and he strikes the nerve, and he swells and the health is grievous, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any homes due to its subtlety, then it behooves you to sound the instrument anesil; and seek out the nerve at your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the fingers, thus they make it two inches long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	Here is the translation:
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Here is the translation:
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it is not limited to just maintaining health and preventing future illnesses; and it should be done in one of the three veins that are on the arm: namely, cephalic, fastidious, and basilic; and one should bloodlet at the beginning of spring, autumn, and winter after eating, when signs of repletion appear; and one should bloodlet on the first or third day, two or three hours after eating.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bloodletting that is administered for illnesses has no fixed hour determined, but rather it is done when the need arises, at any time of day or night; and one must not bloodlet children until 13 years old, nor a woman who is pregnant beyond the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should they cauterize the old who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to bloodlet, in whatever manner it may be, one must first clear the intestines with a gentle laxative, if they retain much flatulence, so that the veins do not attract the superfluous and harmful humors from the principal members; nor should one bloodlet those who are too full of food, or drunk, as long as it is possible, nor those who are dropsical; and one should beware of bloodletting after a passion of the colon, and vomiting, and decay of the stomach, and multiple conceptions in a woman, and labor, and watching, and fasting, and such like things; then subtle the humors, if the blood is gross, by food and drink and medicine, so that you have little power; then enter into a bath, so that nothing may hinder, to subtly clear the blood, and bloodlet from the vein on the third day, as we have said; and guard against that day of labor, and of puncture, and of luxury, and similar things; and be joyful and happy, and let the bloodletter be more skilled than the one who is being bloodletted, and massage the arm twice or three times, then extract the blood moderately, because when it is too constricted or loose, it cannot flow freely; then massage the hand so that the veins swell, and feel them; then moisten the bloodletter with a little oil of violet, then put his left hand on the vein beneath the hand, where he wants to bloodlet, so that the vein does not fail or falter at the touch.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Because there are veins that flee as if they were cords to the healthy person, and if there are those that are full of windiness, so when one puts on the flame, it retreats from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of these; and if one opens the vein, it is because the wound is too narrow, for which reason it is necessary that the surgeons be advised about these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; if not, then recommence a little below that place or on the side, if the veins are not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are swollen, and the patient is in a swoon, let him lie for a day or two, and do not bind his arm: lest by chance abscesses may form; do not enter or bathe, then recommence the treatment as it pleases him; and if the perforation is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that there is not so much blood as you saw, then insert the entire flame directly into that perforation; and make a slight incision hastily, so that the veins are swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	Here is the translation:
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which often occurs, especially when it is not healthy enough to be opened at that time or the opening of the vein is small, then hasten, and put on the limb a wet sponge in water and a little warm, and hold it for an hour; and it is necessary that you do this after the blood issue from the vein, and if it remains on the limb after several days without any blackness or greenness, it does not harm; and if you see, put on something of aloes or myrrh ointment in juice of calament, masterwork, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there occurs an abscess and appearance at the wound of the basilica: put your hand on it, and if you find the soft spot at the compression of the hand, it is that bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid then that you do not put on anything of what we have said, for it may happen in court without an artery; but the physician makes a plaster to harden the spot, then cures with another cure, until it be healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw each one's blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Because the patient's blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it thin out until it becomes subtle; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is full and strong, and has mastery of blood extraction, to make a larger wound, and let the flames be large; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed less often and more slowly, and you must bleed in a slanting cut, not in a piercing way; and this method of bleeding is free from disorder of blood and from copiousness of nerve, and is better than the bleeding of the loins or of the large veins.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to the one whose body is worn out at the health resort, it is necessary to give a warm poultice made from juice of green pomegranates; if they are overheated, then draw three or four times the blood III times or IIII. And if they are of cold complexion, then apply before the health resort a warm poultice made with syrup of musk, or with aromatic honey syrup containing spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and galanga, and well-fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if they faint at the health resort, after the evacuation of much blood, it is necessary that they have a broth of beef, and subtle fragrant syrup, and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of a vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to anoint his arm, and heal another time, it is necessary, when it is weakened by great wound, that he anoints little by little, according to the quantity of its continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And he who wants to anoint his arm after the first healing, and it has a strong course, if he anoints seven hours after the first healing, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And he who wants to heal from another part, if he should anoint on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body which is already overheated, and it causes fever; if you need to draw a large quantity, and widen the opening so that it spurts into a basin; then you must observe all the conditions of health, and place your hand on the pulse when it beats, so that death does not occur in the patient's body, and this happens often, when the healers are negligent; and do not press forcefully upon it when you see the arm relax, and cause blood to issue a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press firmly upon it; nor if it is bent, should it be extended hastily, for that would be bad; but let it beat as long as it bleeds a second time; or you have reached the point of the flame, so that the blood which is congealed at the vein's opening flows forth, and place it in a warm bath, and press upon it gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not constrict it, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to bleed the blood a second time, let it be in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthy in place of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of bloodletting is that the patient puts their hand in warm water, so that the vein becomes red; then it should be bound moderately, so that the vein appears well, then prick now through the middle, not too large nor too long; and let the punctures be wide, and let it be well near the joint of the hand, and if you cannot get it out, then put the hand in warm water again, and let the blood flow into the water, until you have enough; and if it is in winter, do not reuse the hand in warm water, for they put it more in spring than in winter; and the bloodletting of this vein is safer than all other veins, since there is no artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The bloodletting of the salvatory vein of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the method: hold the hand, and put it in warm water, until the vein becomes swollen, so that you can see it; and if you prick now through the middle, and if you cut around entirely, do not grieve anything; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are very close to the flesh, and then put the hand in warm water again, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and cannot get out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn out as much blood as is necessary for the task, then put oil on the vein and sew it up quickly, and thus do for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The health of the hand on the left side is good for the disease of the thigh, and do everything just as I have told you about the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The wisdom of the sophene is worth everything for all the diseases that are beneath the body, such as diseases of the liver, and retention of flowers, and disease of the kidneys, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its wisdom is that the patient feels as if their foot is in hot water, and it pricks at the vein so much that it hurts; and it puts above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many veins; thus sometimes a large vein, or at the ankle, which is more valuable.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you strain above the foot, so beware of the nerves that are underneath, and the vein of traversing as in a coping; and let the flames be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the saneness cannot issue from it, then reset the foot in the water, and let the vein be well purged.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the wisdom fails the first time, it recommences the second above a little, because the joints are salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus make the wisdom of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The joints of the sciatic vein are at the gathering of strength, and its sinew is worth the pain of the hip, when it is because of hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of his sanity is such that the patient goes between the bath, and stretches above the crutch IIII fingers in twisting, for otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then the vein flows in all ways that you can, and across; and it is worth more that you take care of it, for the blood is sound, and it is much restored to many homes.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then the vein of those that open or give two fingers below, and towards the small toe, and beware of the nerves; and make a correction of the blood as you see, and then release the bond, and put on cotton and constrain; it is now healthy.
des sainies de ventouse	of the veins of the cupping glasses
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping is made of horns, or of brass, or of glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and attracting blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is without piercing is done in two ways: either it is with full fire, or without fire; and the cupping that is done by piercing and extraction of blood is done on XIII places of the body, where one is at the top of the head; and another in the neck; and two others in the sides of the neck; and the cupping under the chin; and the cupping of the shoulders; and the cupping on the hips; and the cuppings on the arms; and the cuppings on the legs; and the cuppings on the ankles; and the cupping does not draw blood, except from small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it is not feared, just as one does with vein blood, and it is not necessary that it be administered, neither with full fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, as long as the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of sickness it is necessary to bleed, either by habit or custom, if we delay each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at every time; for there are those who, when they have mastery over bleeding, have a heavy head; and there are those who experience repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and in their neck, and darkness in their eyes; and there are those who spew a mouthful of blood, and have a swollen tongue, and spit out blood; and if there are those who sigh, and see nothing but blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we command to apply a poultice after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The blood of the nose helps with the grief of the head … which comes to their eyes, and it is not fitting that this be after the evacuation of all the body; and this bleeding is in place of the blood of the cephalic, and it is not fitting that one who is of a cold complexion uses it, or has catarrh, for this causes them great harm; and therefore it is not fitting that the veiled ones use it, nor those who have colds or frosts.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are often wounded, if they become obtuse, and therefore it is necessary to put the cupping glass a little lower due to the doubt of obtuseness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation in the neck is in the place of the healthy head and the basilica, and for this reason it has esteem for the straightness of the spine, and for the fracture of the channel of the arm, and for the coughing, and for the replenishment; and it is necessary to avoid breaking, because if it holds too firmly, it injures the obliance or stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilations as the ribs of the neck have esteem for the pains of the head, and obtalmia and emigration, and for the strangulation, and for the pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in the place of the healthiness of the basilica; and it is necessary that you instruct the healthy one to press his hand to put, so he does not touch the artery, and does not show signs of bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The winds below the chin affect the mouth disease, and corruption of gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the vein of the .ij. lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilations of the back are worth an illness that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventilations of the joints have esteem as much as the three veins of the arm, because it attracts blood from these large veins; and instruct the healthy one to not make too many deep wounds, because the limbs are nourished by flesh, and know about the underlying nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping that is on the back is like emerods of deep foundation, and like diseases below, and it is necessary that the cupping be large, and be of iron, so it has mastery to treat well; and by chance, if it were subtle, it would break; and it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cuppings of the legs feel openly, because they attract blood from all over the body, and are worth as ancient pains of the kidneys, and of the liver, and of the bladder, and recall the flowers; and are in the place of .ij. soporifics, and of .ij. chevilles, and altogether they enfeeble the body after long use, and bring about palsy in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the cupping is that you put it on first empty, and suck at once, and put it on hastily, and move evenly, and do not cease from doing so, until you see the place red and swollen, and feel the flow of blood; then firm, and reapply the cuppings, and take heed in the disposition of the body, for there are those who have tender flesh, and clear pores: if it is necessary to pierce once softly, and make large wounds, and a little deeply; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is abundant, it is necessary to pierce .ij. times: the first time to subtly open the way for the abundant blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it must be cauterized a third time; and when we want to draw out a little blood by little, it suffices to hold it back only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to remove much blood, we recommend often; and if the blood is thick, we make a strong fontanel, and the ends are such that the coursing should be perceived suddenly, and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have obstructed pores, that you apply the leeches of oil apertif and dissolutif: if it is in summer, of violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucumber seed oil; and if it is in winter, of cress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superficies are large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of balsamite, or oil of anise, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if there are those who have tender skin and large pores, it is not necessary to put on oil, but it is necessary to wash after the ventosation of rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from ajueil, or from the water of myrtle, and of sumac, and of similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have swollen superfluities rise from wine, or from water of rue, or from a decoction of anet or chamomile, or from similar things; and it is not suitable to apply a cupping glass before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and one must not sleep after the cupping, and it is necessary that they warn themselves when they should be cupped and when they are cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware of those who are healthy but choleric, and their blood is too agitated and inflamed; if it is necessary that they take cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuce in the shade, and similar things; and they should eat little pucins, and flesh of young roosters, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, should take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat little pucins and small birds and pigeons; and on the day they are cupped, they should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give to some men three or four muscatels before cupping, or after, to comfort the principal members; and let the blood be subtle, but it is not suitable that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Here is the translation:
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cupping glass administered by fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And have two large and a half palm in front, and have the costal bone touched near the small perforation, like one would pierce with a needle, and be of iron or steel, to put a bandage in place, and have in the middle a transverse rod of iron or steel, to apply a compress, and they are large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them; for the blisters of children are different from those of the old, and of the thin than the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must then place this bandage on the limb: take the compress of wax or linen, and put it in the bandage across the rod that is in the bandage, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the bandage so it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the limb, and these two are on the perforation as we have said, so that when one wants, if the vapor goes away, and one removes the bandage; and take the linen again as before, and reapply it often, if you have mastery.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping that is administered in disease of the lungs, to all aching, it has no strength nor pertussis, and is not administered unless when it is full of water, and is placed on the limb only slightly; and this is its form.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Cupping is not administered unless on members where one cannot place cups due to their smallness, such as eyelids and cheeks, and similar places; and in denuded skin of flesh, such as fingers or toes, and similar things; and the quality of the usage is that when you find cuppings that are in sweet gentle waters without purification, if they take them; and put a nut in sweet water, so they become familiar, and have nothing in their belly; and then be healthy from vein and cupping, then rub the limb until it becomes red, and place on the cuppings; and when they will be full, and will cling, this is where one can place a cup, if one puts it, for it is worth much afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	Here is the translation:
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not take, then rub the wound with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle so that the wound is opened, and then put them back, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will adhere; and when you see that they are closing, sprinkle a little powder of alum, sage, or cinder, which will make them heal now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here is the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish wise men stray from this chapter, for they never read any of the ancient books, nor did they learn a single letter; and for this reason is the science strange in our land, for I never found any good in it; and I know nothing, except through the science of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the experience of my life; and I have described to you here in this chapter what is contained, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are mentioned, as I did in those two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary therefore that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the words and the chapters where wisdom places its understanding, and dwells on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or bruising occurs to anyone, it is necessary that you hurry to heal the patient from one part and another, so that nothing prevents them entirely, as weakness of the body, or infancy, or old age; or if the tension is not very strong, or too cold; and avoid cold joints, this means to know cold joints, and the flesh of birds and goats, and do not drink wine, nor eat coarse rough meat, and do not overfill with foods that fill the veins with blood, so you have no doubt about abscess heating up, nor spreading of matter in the limb; if you regain the patient according to their primary government which they used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to restore, it is necessary that you nourish the patient with meats that make great nourishment, or if they have viscosity, as if they were fed on thick soup, and rice, and bread, and pieces of meat, and bacon, and eggs, and fresh fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For a good nourishment represents marrow and more quickly heals the break.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well rejoined or reunited according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but there is no cure, reset the broken bone with a large splint which separates and joins the limb together, so it enforces as it was before; and do not overwork them at all, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish them with coarse foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	Here is the translation:
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it breaks with a wound, and breaks at all a small notch.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And in each manner he has his engine, and his proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory brings back to its place; and it is known that the breakage of the bone occurs because the bones are twisted, and appears well by palpation, and sounds at the pressing of the hand; and when there is no tortuosity in his touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no point of breakage; but he can have tortuosity, or crack, or small breakage.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It does not matter if you move the hand, but apply medicines that come here afterwards, and then hold it steady now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the breakage that goes into a cavity, and are the two disjointed parts, they must now be put in equal alignment, so that the abscesses will not grow; and if the abscesses grow, let it alone for a while, until the abscesses are appeased; then set them in place so you can gently and wisely touch, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than the restorations of those where there are pieces; then hold steady, as it is necessary after.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, whether it is the second part, whether it is hand or foot, or with your hand if it is a small limb, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand; and put the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are disjoined, you reset them by all means in their proper places as you can, and take care through your work not to come to the patient with injury or pain; and adjust well the two heads of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels well in his hand if it seems to him that it is not well: if it is straightened nicely, and not strained too much, nor pressed as those who come with their work of abscess and contraction in the limb, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in a point, chastise well the patient so they do not move it, neither while awake nor while asleep, nor while turning, nor in any other way; and take care that the limb is so stabilized that they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when they feel no pain, it is not in a point, and you must put it in such disposition that they feel no pain; and take care that it is set straight, so that twisting does not come when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Here is the translation:
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is inflammation or abscess, put an aposteme-chasing ointment on it, which draws out the inflammation, and leaves it thus for a few days; then hold your fingers steady, and be in the middle of a large cane reeds gathering, or of wood where they make the clevis, or of palm reeds, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the instrument which one puts on the fracture be a little larger and wider than the others; and be as long as it is necessary for the member of smallness or greatness; then hold your fingers steady, just as you did at first, then tie above with a thread, just as in the first instance on the fracture; the tighter it is, the less; and it is necessary that the thread be moderate, not too large nor too small, and be of flaxen cord; for if the threads are large, like I have seen of the foolish people who make their ligatures with twisted cords, it is a great error, because the ligature cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and does not allow that there be less than two fingers' breadth between each instrument.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patients are injured by the staples after the constriction in their healthy areas, then put under them swabs of linen or a layer of paper, so that they do not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the breakage, and the course is broken, I will tell you the treatment following this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not suit to stretch out the broken limbs on the first day.
