Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Here is the translation:
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to restore the fracture and dislocation and twisting: take abrasives and ladanium and enula and asa fetida and Arabic gum and mugwort, ana .x. З.; myrrh and aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; and make a powder, and mix with egg white; if the patient's complexion is warm, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and helps many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of plastering that is good for torsion: take mugwort and vismalve, in the shape of an X; mix and blend, in the shape of VIII; add acaice VI; boil Armenian bole X, and crush well, and concoct with water or abundant egg whites, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way of plastering for joints and dislocated bones, and to calm the sudden pain, and to reduce the swelling of the bone, and the fracture: take new flax, and grind it into a poultice in warm water and oil, and apply it to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore at all, but they are good for calming hot abscesses, and properly reducing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to apply plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and earth-based peony leaves, and crush them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way of plastering for the restoration of bone fractures and to diminish the remainder of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Here is the translation:
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of applying it more forcibly than the first, when a stubborn abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of vismalve, and seeds of lin, balauste, mellilote, and sansuce, and flowers of violets and camomille, all in one part; and crush, and mix with water of salt, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the warmth of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Here is the translation:
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that one should apply to the broken member, to restore it, things dried and a little warm, like myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to apply is good for a lesion and pain: take mugwort and decapitate the heads of men, or feathers of a bird, and visnaga, and adjust similarly, and crush, and make an application on the affected member.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then undo it a little afterwards, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor is the bone out of its place; if you undo it too soon and pain comes to the limb, or inflammation, without rest or swelling, hasten it, and undo it, and remove the application now; and take a lighter dressing, and sponge with seawater, and dip in water, and lift up the limb, until the inflammation ceases, and the pain is appeased; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on a dry or oiled cloth, and bind it with a nut, until you are certain of a hot abscess; and remove the inflammation of the limb, and be rid of the pain, then resume the subtle treatment, and a little application, and do not strain it too much as before; and continue subtly until it is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen, and you have need of emplastering and bandaging, then resume it, as you did initially for the first treatment.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb of what we have said, do not dislodge further until after three days or four or five or seven; and no time leave it for twenty days, according to what one sees, until the bruise appears, and approaches the adjustment of the flesh underneath; then restrain more than before, and it thickens its meat, as I have said before; and if you see the limb drying out more than is necessary, know that nourishment cannot come; arose from the warm water treatment, all the times you dislodge it, and this is each tier day, and ease a little the ligature; by this work then corrects the nourishment to the limb, and immediately amends what the foolish mirror shows, which restores the limb crookedly: it is bad, and if it is perverse works, I do not see another thing but to leave it and open it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of fractures, and diverse shapes, and the causes are destined; for there are fractures that are made by percussion of a spear, and the neck bone breaks all the bone just up to the socket which is beneath the bone, as if it were shattered or crushed; and because of this, this kind of fracture is called "shattering".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Where the spear cuts through the bone from above, piercing senselessly, and this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; and it is the wound of these two great or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or fissure, or break in the neck of the stone, or fall on the stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if he has a persistent bruise that approaches just below the skin which is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and it is this wound whether large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound that is placed in the bone as subtly as a hair, and the crack is small, and because of this it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound that is made or by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by similar thing, and makes the piece of the bone go down, and the bones are joined together like the cauldron when they are melted over the cauldrons; thus between the stones within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And it happens more to those who have moist bones, like the bone of a child; and there are all these kinds of fracture where small pieces are disjoined as if they were shattered; and I will speak of them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all ways of breaks by the traction on them, and the inquiry with tension, and by the corrupt flesh that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The similarity of the hairline is known by this, that when one discovers the bone, and one rubs on it, then the black break appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of breaks, beware of accidents that harm the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and extension, and numbness, and fever and ague, and the eyes issuing forth and reddening, and other similar things in worse dispositions, it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a sudden accident, and you expect healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the naval disease comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to open the bone before the fourteenth day of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to open the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue under the bone does not become corrupted, and the accidents we have mentioned do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the break of the bone reaches to the membrane that covers the brain, so it is necessary that you split the affected part in this way: and it is that you take hold of the chief of the wounded head, and uncover on the bone in all ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more subtle than you can, and if a flow of blood comes to uncover the bone, or an abscess falls, so it is necessary that you aid with what you need, and it is that you fill the hole with medicated ointments; and make the wound rest until the abscess is appeased, and be assured of the flow of blood; then begin to osteotomize around the bone, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method is that you cut straight beforehand, and it is the form.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I make another cut, larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have a number of diverse cuts, some straight and others wide, and are pointed, and are of iron indeed; and in working lightly, so that you do not blister the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is necessary that you pierce around, thus you will administer gentle touches with tapers, not too deeply so they do not penetrate beyond the bone, and must have a margin or circle above, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must have more, if each one returns to its place according to the width of the bone, if you have tapers for every test; and it is the form of the three manners of tapers.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality of piercing around the broken bone is that you put a taper on the bone, and turn your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced; then put the taper in another place a little later, and do it all around, then cut into the space of the bone which is between the perforations, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you extract the bone with your hand, or with one of the instruments you have, such as pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the spleen.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone, and extracted, it is necessary that you reuse the instrument which is remaining from the bone to all other similar instruments, but it is necessary that it be more delicate and more subtle than the other incising tools; and if there remains nothing of small bones, no scales, so lift them lightly with one of the instruments; then cure the wound with tents and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another manner of surgery is that which Galien says, which is more wise; and he praises it highly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you discover a part of the bone, there where the break appears, so that when you have discovered that part, then put below the head of this incisional instrument, whose form is:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one part, and the affected area is on the II rib, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then make a small incision above, so that you can easily cut around the entire bone, and take good care of the membrane that is beneath; if it is attached to the bone, cut easily around it, for one cuts well without hurting, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not penetrate up to the membrane, and the bone is so badly broken above, and there are small pieces, thus it is necessary to remove that asperity, and to extract the scales at the subtle raspings you must have diverse quantities, to arrange in each place the most convenient, according to the work and figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you rasp beforehand with large raspings, and afterwards with more subtle ones, and do not cease from doing that until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-like fractures and subtle breaks, it is necessary that you arrange the cause according to its direction; and this is a thing that is not readily apparent to one who has not put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the swelling is uncovered, it is necessary that you apply a linen cloth according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it with rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another doubled cloth in II or III, and moisten it with wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, so as not to irritate the swelling, then apply above another layer, and do not constrict it more than necessary so that it touches the wound solely; and leave it thus for a day or II, until the abscesses are appeased, then remove them, and administer medicines such as roots of plants, and flour of vegetables, and powdered incense, and aristologe, and similar things; and make powder from these things, and place on the wound, and administer medicines without causing numbness; and be careful that the wound is properly clean, so you do not leave any suppurating matter, nor assemble a poultice, for when a poultice assembles on the membrane of the brain, it corrodes and putrefies, and brings great harm to the patient; for when you apply something caustic to the swelling, it increases by adding above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Here is the translation:
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackness does not come forth by means of the medicine that one has applied, it is necessary that you take a part of honey and three parts of oil of rose and glue in the drapal; then apply the cure in many ways as it is fitting, until it be healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that often the two parts of the nail are broken above, or one part by the joint, for they are two bones; and the one beneath is cartilaginous, and does not break, so it does not make a swelling or twisting, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you bind your small finger or toes with thread, and put the same breakage therein according to your natural finger index, and in the pouch by deficiency, until the nail regains its natural shape; and do this lightly, and beware that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nail, and cannot come to the joint, then it is necessary that you put it even at the head of a slightly large vein.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the breakage is of two parts, do another similarly, and hasten to restore on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the aposteme's heat is appeased, then bind at the tip of the nail with threads of linen, if the breakage is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Where you touch another part, the break is there; and let the tents be so thick that they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that one must soak the tents in a mixture, and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be soaked in a concoction of egg white and powdered millet; then leave the tents alone until the bone is firm, and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes touch where the wing of an eagle is in place of tents, and if there is a soft drapery inside, and it holds the break, and soothes the patient within; or do what you have seen.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose while you operate, if you meet cerate or cotton softened in rose oil, or in a little pouch of dragon's blood.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if apostemes (abscesses) come, apply a plaster made from flour of sisament and powdered incense, mixed with egg white, then place light poultices, and do not bind the knee; and if the break in the knee is small, and it is broken into little pieces, extract them as comfortable stromens to that, then cut the fissure, and treat the things causing anguish there, and soon, as one applies comfortable plasters and ointments to that; and if there are no inner wounds on the knee, apply treatment to the tents, and place canes of lead, until it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is dislocated downwards, and there is no point of injury beforehand, and the break is dislocated so slightly, and it does not break into two, unless the cartilage within is crushed, if one recognizes it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is in the right part, that you put your right index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the break is in the left jawbone, then put your right index finger, and gently put the break into place, and hold it with the other hand from behind, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jawbone is dislocated inwards, it is necessary that you administer extension from inwards, as much as it becomes even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movements of the teeth occur, or fracture, if you restrain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on the broken jawbone a cerote, and put on it a double wrapping; and put on the wrapping a large and well-made staple, or a piece of even leather, long and wide according to the jawbone, and bind it to the mouth that you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see the figure changing, dislocate it on the third day, and then reset to the point where it changed; and apply a poultice made with powder from the mill with abundant water or flour of six-month-old wheat, after you have removed the crust; and apply a light poultice, and if the poultices are effective, and the disposition of the patient does not change, let it be until it is healthy; many times it heals in twenty-two days.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses occur, treat them according to what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reset the broken bone in its place; if you subtly remove the extraneous bits that are not necessary to the bone.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is constricted, expand it with flame according to the necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have gathered all these pieces, and there is no delay, then cauterize the wound, if it is large, and apply suitable poultices to that, in order to heal the flesh, so that it may be healthy.
de la forcele	of the stronghold
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The stronghold breaks more often beforehand, towards the shoulder, and the break is in three ways: either it is broken and dislocated in two places, and there are pieces, and it is easier to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operations are when the break is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the shoulder that feels the stronghold broken; and the other stretches out the neck towards the part; then sets the break in your hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have to treat more extensively, then place under the patient's shoulder a round sphere of cloth or leather, and let it be thick according to your need; and steady and lift the forceps, and hold the sphere with your hand, so that you set the fracture evenly.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot manage the head of the forceps at the forefront, because it comes in the opposite direction, then it is necessary that the patient leans back on their hinder part, and place under the shoulder a small pillow, and push the minister's shoulder down, until the bone of the forceps is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then adjust the fracture with your fingers, and if you feel roughness, it is necessary that you bend over; and draw out the lighter pieces, and if the bone cannot join due to any prominence, take one of the incisors you have; but place under the forceps this instrument, to ward off the swelling.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it seems a spoon, and is not a measuring device, and be as large as the hollow of the bone and the power of the veins; and have two heads, if you see, and one is large, and the other is narrow, like the routing of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are assured of a hot abscess, cut into the wound, and if the routing is small, or you doubt hot abscess, fill the wound with drapnels and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the hot abscess comes, apply a dressing with oil of roses and in vinegar and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The strapping of the bone, when it is without wounds and without damage, is that you put on the bone the plaster made from powdered millstone and egg whites, and lightly apply it, and place a splint underneath, so you have mastery over it; then take a very large bandage a palm's length wide, then apply double layer of gauze over the strapping; then take a subtle steel instrument three finger-widths long and narrow, and wrap it around that bandage, so the head of the bandage hangs down; and place the instrument on the break, and turn the bandage around the neck, and underneath the healthy skin, and underneath the diseased skin; and adjust each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the break firmly, and you clearly see that the instrument does not move over the broken bone, then reward it every day, and when the ligatures relax, then restrain it; and make the patient lie on their back, and put a small pillow underneath, to raise the shoulder high; if you lighten the fracture of the arm by lightening the shoulder, or you bind the arm to the neck, and no bad accident happens, until twenty days; then restart the strapping, if you see that it is necessary, and restrain it and leave it thus, until it is restored; and it will be restored in twenty-eight days at most, and for some people in less time.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Here is the translation:
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone protrudes forward, and not below the heart, if it is above, and the bone, and do as we have said in the breaking of the forced abscess to appease.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it breaks often at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken within, it declines to the lowest part, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks strength, and everything, and by chance vomits blood, and opens the passages in the broken bone, and the wound seems well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back, and you put a cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and assemble the ribs of the sides with your hands, and subtly adjust to make it even in all ways that you can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; then put on plasters and bandages of subtle salt water, or other lighter dressing, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the round ligament to the back, and hold it firmly, and reward every hour the treatment, and if it is restored, then restrain it; and if it is loosened, due to corrosion or pus that comes from the wound, or pain or abscess, hasten, and loosen, and remove the plaster, and address what has come in ways of cures; then restore the plaster, and hold it firm until it is healthy.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	You know that the breaking of the ribs only occurs because they are large behind the back, and at the inner head, and do not bend except when they are slippery; and one feels it well during the inquiry in both.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restorers are that you make equal the fracture, as it is fitting.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and hold it in place with a bandage, so that you have mastery over it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of the ribs declines inward, the patient feels very great pain, and numbness, just as with pleurisy, because the bone touches the membrane; and it reaches to the points, and all and vomits greatly, and it is a grievous wound, and the old men have put great effort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that they need to administer foods that inflame the stomach, in order to relieve the breathlessness at the time of the fever.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, because hot abscesses do not come to life, if they have not arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has arrived, then bleed it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that one should not place ventouses on the skin, to suck out the bad humor, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt whether the ventouse attracts the excess humors from the skin due to its weak disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they instruct to cover the limb of a bruised ankle in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to set the ligature evenly, then it is cured by the treatment of pleurisy, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear due to the bone that touches the fabric, and doubt is in the patient, then it is fitting to cut above the broken rib, and it is fitting to put an instrument underneath to ward off the blood; and then one must incise the bone, and treat lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and cure with plasters, until they are healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come, put warm millet porridge on it with rose oil, and apply it to the affected area; and treat while the area is being prepared for the abscess, and be careful not to touch the surrounding skin where it should be, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	of the breakage of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a breakage comes to the bone of the neck, and soon it happens that it breaks; and also it has a curvature of the spine.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when it happens to anyone, and you want to know if they will be healthy or not, take heed if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortally wounded in many dispositions, and if they move and feel well when they are held firmly and steadily, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient's illness is cured, so one can put them to treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you want to know if they will be healthy or not, take heed if the feet are softened, and if the accident is in their hands, and on their back there is windiness and involuntary evacuation; and when one has evacuated it from their belly, then there is involuntary evacuation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is swooning on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: do not labor in vain during his care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, it is the lightest thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you apply if there is a hot abscess, apply to the spine oil of rose or oil of rue, as much as it is alleviated; then apply one of the comforting and drying emplasters, and bind with a lien, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that side where they feel the pain, until they are healthy.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bone becomes dislocated, it is necessary to cover over the heart; and take out the bone, then assemble the .ij. lips of the wound, so that it is large, in a stitch, then the treatment with ointment, healing the flesh as much as possible; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the hip", you put your pouched hand on the left, and place it evenly on the other hand at your power, then put the plaster and the staple above, so that you have mastery; then hold steady, and if there is a dislocated bone, make it thus, and take out, and treat the wound until it is healthy.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the thigh
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Because the bone of the thigh is broken, and if it is, then there will not be a small amount of diminishment at the head; and make a long bandage, and decline to the partitions, and comes to the patient's pain in the leg, and swelling, and inflames what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as much as you are above the fracture; and know what the fracture and the shape of it are; and if the fracture is at the head only, then put evenly on that fracture, so that it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is too long, or it declines inward, then make the patient sit on his stomach, so that the restoration of this break may be apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it straight, put on the plaster, then put on a stick of wood or of oak, and hold the break steady, so that it does not move; and apply the poultice beneath the ribs, until the ligature is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes, do not touch it, until the abscess is appeased, and put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and hold it as it is necessary, so that there is no bad accident; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The joints are those that are between the neck and the head of the shoulder, and if it is fractured, one must restore it according to one of the following methods: one of which is that you take a full moleskin plaster, according to this form.
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And lay the joints in a high place, and sit the patient on a chair; then you put a broken arm on a wooden splint, until it reaches the armpit, and has a curve of wood, then place on some heavy thing or the ministers extend downwards; then put the mirrors to adjust the fracture equally with his hands together, until the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you support the patient on his shoulder, and tie the hand to his neck, then command the ministers that one holds what is on the fracture with his hands, and the others hold underneath all the joints, and extend each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forced, hold the bone below the fracture, and on the fracture, and extend each of the ministrations to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the head of the shoulder, it is necessary that you put the bone mean below the socket, and the other towards the joint, below the fracture; and also if the fracture is towards the joint, it is necessary to put the bone lightly, without labor, until the fracture is even on its place, and on the joint; then set the fracture right, as it is necessary, and hold steady, so that apostemes do not come there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses come, do not hold steady for seven days, and put on a soft, moist cloth in oil and rose water, until the abscesses are appeased; then hold steady, and the manner of holding is that you place the dressing on the breakage, then assemble the arm on the joint, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and place the bandage, and hold steady on the joint, and on the arm, so that the arm is in a state of rest, so that nothing disturbs it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use a splint, and place on the breakage a splint larger and stronger than the others, and have between each splint two fingers of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes over the breakage two fingers from each part; then hold steady with the splints, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the breakage, more strongly and less in opposition.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the alignment of the stars and the constriction, as we have said, while you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, let it stay until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at each of them for three days to see that no swelling comes to the limb, or the nourishments cannot come to the limb because it is too constricted.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you hasten, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, do not undo the dressing until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and put his hands on his stomach; and place under the shoulder a plain cushion of equal thickness, and look every hour of the day or night, that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or the bonds are not loosened; hasten it by the power of medicine, and give him the food that we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is at first subtle; and when he begins to recover, let it be abundant.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be restored to health within 40 days of treatment; and then one must dislodge and administer baths and medications for the joints to realign.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is lazy and swollen, it takes 10 days or 2 months to dislodge.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of 18 bones, which are called the "foscile", of which one is small, and it is the one that joins the pouchet; and the other is large, and it is the one that is underneath, towards the little finger; by chance breaking the large foscile solely, or the small one, and by chance they both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small fractures are broken, the restorations are light, and the healings; and when the large ones are broken, the healing is bad, and worse than when they are broken and united together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it's a small fracture that's only slightly broken, then one must extend it lightly, and set it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it's a large fracture, then one must stretch it more strongly; and extend it on a cushion, and tie the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the small fingers lower than the others, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the ministrations like an arm to the part below his hand, or at the lien, and another ministration above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he puts the mirrors equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, then put each one in its place, and if there is no dislocation that pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then fix it thus and the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the breaking of a wound, I have spoken of it to the singular chapter; if you take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And at the beginning of the restoration, abscesses and wounds occur, if you apply a plaster made of oil rose and white wax, which should not be too hard nor too soft; and you apply the plaster subtly, until the abscesses and wounds are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the wax, and apply a plaster made of powdered millet with abundant egg whites, then put in the staves, and let the stave for the fracture be stronger and a little larger than the others; and know that it must have six staves or arms in more dispositions: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; and hold more steady on the fracture than other parts, and less often in alignment, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages that are on the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread, which it is strained from linen, not too large nor too small, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And rewind the limb and the ligament after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accident happens to the limb, as if a bruise comes to the limb, it is necessary that you apply warm water to the limb, until the bruises are soothed; and let the limb not be tightly restrained, but rather rested.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the strapping, and if the ligaments are softened and the bones are disjointed, and similar things, so adjust it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care that the numbness does not come to the limb, because it is too constricted, then it is necessary that you loosen it a little, and let it be for some days, until the numbness is corrected, and then it will be restrained.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, do not undo the dressing until 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	where he turns inward, then places his hands on his neck, and makes his neck even, and guards against movement and degeneration, and sleeps on his back; and knows that this fracture is restored in 30 days or in 35, and perhaps by chance in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexities of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You know that on the back of the hand and as we have few fractures, and it does not come but rather frequent sprains.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the finger of the hand is broken or sprained, it is necessary that the patient sits crossed, and sits directly in front of him evenly; then put his hand on the extended toe, and extend the ministres the broken bones, and set them even with the mirrors, so they are well joined; and apply the plaster and bandages, if abscesses come, then put a splint according to the quantity of the swelling; and be enveloped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is at the base of the thumb near the belly of the palm, make a sphere of bandages, and instruct the patient to hold it against their broken thumb; and then bind with a long bandage, and let it be the splint of soft leather as big as the thumb of the hand, and bind it, as it is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the forearm, it is necessary that you put a splint on top, and another below in the palm, so that the hand is covered and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and tighten the ligature between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture occurs in one of the fingers, it is the pouch that makes it equal, as it is necessary; and bind it with the palm, and see if you put a small straight splint to lift the fracture, and do not move; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, as in the index or one of the others, make it equal, and bind it with the healthy finger that comes after; or you bind them all together, that makes them steady, or you put a splint on top, as in a pouch; and take care in the restoration and in the disposition of hot abscesses, and heal what has come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the hip is often broken, and it is clearly seen when it twists in front and behind; and the restoration is done by binding the ligature above the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient puts it on his face, then each minister extends his bandage to its equal part; and it's when the fracture is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the thigh, then let one of the ligaments be towards the finger, and the other ligaments below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is close to the knee, and then let the ligaments be towards the knee, and the extension below; then put the mirrors to make the bone equal with his two hands, so that it is according to its natural figure, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, if abscesses come from there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it cool down and then return to your work and your treatment; the lieure is done in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you envelop the fracture with a doubled bandage in two or three layers, and remove the superfluous parts, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the nail, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and make the head of the thread above; then turn the bandage on the leg and on the thigh, then put these straps on the fracture, and put a strap on the bone of the leg; then fill in the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft drapery to equalize the constriction, then start to bind firmly three or four times around the fracture; and when you go further up from the fracture, there is less constriction; then take as two heads of the thread that you put between the leg and the thigh, and in three straps that are above, then return below to the head of the thread, so that you come out at the foot; and hold it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, so that there comes no abscess or swelling or other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, if it dislocates, and address what comes from it, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, then it must be extracted, whoever can; and if they cannot, then it must be broken, and forced out; and the treatment is as we have said, until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And no time is the joint broken thus that one puts them back, as in the joint and in the arm; nevertheless, in the restoration made thus it does not shut out the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the joint is restored to its place, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the gutter of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the groove of the knee joint there is little bruising, but it often collapses.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it's not just a crack, or an opening, and it has a complete wound, and feels a wound, and this feels very bad.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when one puts back in place what is crooked in its two joints, so that it is assembled as one can; then put on the plaster, and one puts a round stave, if you are skilled in this, and hold steady as it suits, then rewind all the arrangements that we have said in other fractures, as for hot abscesses and similar things; if one puts back in place what suits each accident, so that it is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called "mustelz" by right, and the other is called "foscile"; and it has all the same breaks as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is just like that of the arm equally, and the work is all the same. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg becomes twisted in every part.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, they turn forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, it feels great pain, and one sees it well; and it twists then.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then one should apply extension, and make it even, and lay the splints evenly; but nevertheless, it is necessary that the break is gentle, and there are many pieces, so that the extension may be smaller and lighter; and adjust according to your strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two wooden splints that surround the leg on one side and the other, and are as long as the leg from the knee down to the foot; then wrap them in two layers of bandages above and below, and bind them in the middle, so that the leg cannot decline either to the right or to the left, and thus it is good; and no one should remove the wooden splints for the length of the leg, and it is made of wood, and they put it on the leg to prevent movement, and properly done it heals the broken bone where there is a wound; and move the leg every day to see if there is an abscess or another accident; so cure until it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the breakage of the bones in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there comes no break, but sometimes two bones come to a break and sometimes two poxes, and it does not happen except in more dispositions.
